    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The formyl group may not provide effective coordination or stabilization. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of this group may destabilize the catalyst interaction. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][C]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and electron-donating group
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 5: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 6: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][O][C][O][C]'],  # Rule 9: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Hydroxyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[n][NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 12: Pyridine ring and amino group
        ['[c][nH]'],  # Rule 13: Indole group
        ['[c][CH2Br]'],  # Rule 14: Bromomethyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Hydroxyl and carboxylic acid on phenyl ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 3, 4, 7, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and electron-donating group
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 5: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 6: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][O][C][O][C]'],  # Rule 9: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Hydroxyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[n][NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 12: Pyridine ring and amino group
        ['[c][nH]'],  # Rule 13: Indole group
        ['[c][CH2Br]'],  # Rule 14: Bromomethyl group on aromatic ring

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and electron-donating group
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 5: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 6: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][O][C][O][C]'],  # Rule 9: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Hydroxyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[n][NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 12: Pyridine ring and amino group
        ['[c][nH]'],  # Rule 13: Indole group
        ['[c][CH2Br]'],  # Rule 14: Bromomethyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Hydroxyl and carboxylic acid on phenyl ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 3, 4, 7, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

ML Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy, reaching 0.6571, which is an improvement from the previous lower accuracies (e.g., 0.5714 and 0.6). This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective in capturing the underlying patterns in the data.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent improvement in validation accuracy without a significant drop in performance suggests that the model is not overfitting. However, the relatively low accuracy indicates potential underfitting, suggesting that the rules may not be capturing all the necessary features or interactions.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 3 often has a high positive SHAP value, indicating it might be overestimating the loading. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 3 also shows negative SHAP values, suggesting it might be underestimating the loading in some cases.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy from previous iterations suggests that the rules are improving. However, the accuracy is still below optimal, indicating room for further refinement.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that Rule 3, which involves modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, is influential in both overestimating and underestimating loadings. This suggests that the rule might need refinement to better capture the conditions under which these modifiers lead to high or low loadings.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rule 3:**
   - Given its significant impact on SHAP values, Rule 3 should be refined to better distinguish between cases where multiple hydroxyl groups lead to high versus low loadings. Consider incorporating additional conditions or interactions with other functional groups that might influence the outcome.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values should be examined. This includes Rule 5 and Rule 8, which might need adjustments to better capture the conditions leading to high loadings.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider expanding the feature set or incorporating additional rules that capture more complex interactions. This could involve exploring new functional groups or structural motifs that might influence catalyst loading.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values (positive or negative) and explore ways to adjust them to better align with experimental outcomes.

5. **Incorporate Additional Data:**
   - If possible, incorporate additional data or features that might provide more context or information about the modifiers and their interactions with catalysts. This could help improve the model's ability to generalize and capture more nuanced patterns.

By focusing on these areas, the rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, leading to better predictions of catalyst loading.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][C]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid and electron-donating group
        ['[OX2H][C][OX2H][C][OX2H][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 5: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 6: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Pyridine ring with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][O][C][O][C]'],  # Rule 9: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Hydroxyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[n][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 12: Pyridine ring with amino group
        ['[c][nH]'],  # Rule 13: Indole group
        ['[c][CH2Br]'],  # Rule 14: Bromomethyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Hydroxyl group on phenyl ring with carboxylic acid
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 3, 4, 7, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

    rules = [

**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][C]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid and electron-donating group
        ['[OX2H][C][OX2H][C][OX2H][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 5: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 6: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Pyridine ring with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][O][C][O][C]'],  # Rule 9: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Hydroxyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[n][NX3H2]'],  # Rule 12: Pyridine ring with amino group
        ['[c][nH]'],  # Rule 13: Indole group
        ['[c][CH2Br]'],  # Rule 14: Bromomethyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Hydroxyl group on phenyl ring with carboxylic acid
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 3, 4, 7, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 13) might be contributing to underestimation.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid. (Re-evaluated to focus on specific sulfur-containing structures that consistently show high yield.)

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and methyl
        ['[OX2H][C;R5][C;R5][C;R5][C;R5]'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfur-containing group and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 5: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 6: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][C;X4][OX2][C;X4][OX2]'],  # Rule 9: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Hydroxyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[n][c][NX3;H2]'],  # Rule 12: Pyridine with amino group
        ['[c][nH]'],  # Rule 13: Indole group
        ['[c][CH2Br]'],  # Rule 14: Bromomethyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Hydroxyl and carboxylic acid on phenyl
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 3, 4, 7, 12, 13, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (-COOH) and an amino group (-NH2) tend to result in high yield. This combination likely enhances coordination with metal centers, improving catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2S)-2-aminobutanedioic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid group and an electron-donating group (e.g., methyl) tend to result in low yield. The steric hindrance and electronic effects may hinder effective coordination. Examples: 4-methylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure with at least four hydroxyl groups, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form multiple hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfur-containing group (e.g., sulfanyl) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The sulfur atom may provide additional coordination sites or influence the electronic properties of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (-NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. These groups can alter the electronic environment, potentially enhancing the catalytic activity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains (e.g., octanoic acid, 7-aminoheptanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The hydrophobic nature and steric bulk of long chains may interfere with effective catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers containing a pyridine ring with additional functional groups like carboxylic acids tend to result in high yield. The pyridine's ability to coordinate with metal centers may enhance reactivity. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (-CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless additional stabilizing groups such as amino or hydroxyl groups are present. Examples: 4-formylbenzoic acid (low yield), 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid (low yield).

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., polyether chains) tend to result in low yield. The flexibility and potential steric hindrance of these chains may reduce effective interaction with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on an aromatic ring, without additional electron-withdrawing groups, tend to result in low yield. The hydroxyl group alone may not provide sufficient coordination or electronic influence. Example: 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (-CF3) tend to result in low yield unless paired with other electron-donating groups that could balance the electronic effects. Example: 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an amino group tend to result in high yield. The combination of pyridine's coordination ability and the amino group's potential for hydrogen bonding may enhance catalyst performance. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an indole group tend to result in high yield. The indole's aromaticity and potential for -stacking interactions may stabilize the catalyst. Example: (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a bromomethyl group attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The bromine atom may enhance coordination through halogen bonding. Example: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group on a phenyl ring and an additional carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of hydrogen bonding and potential coordination sites may stabilize the catalyst. Example: 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------
